  /** Converts a <button> to look like an <a> tag. */
  .linkify {
    display: inline;
    padding: 0;
    margin: 0;
    border: 0;
    background: 0;
    cursor: pointer;
  }
  h1, h2, h3, h4 {
    background: none;
  }
  a, chops-button, a.button, .button, .linkify {
    color: var(--chops-link-color);
    text-decoration: none;
    font-weight: var(--chops-link-font-weight);
    font-family: var(--chops-font-family);
  }
  a:hover, .linkify:hover {
    text-decoration: underline;
  }
  a.button, .button {
    /* Links that look like buttons. */
    display: inline-flex;
    align-items: center;
    justify-content: center;
    text-decoration: none;
    transition: filter 0.3s ease-in-out, box-shadow 0.3s ease-in-out;
  }
  a.button:hover, .button:hover {
    filter: brightness(95%);
  }
  chops-button, a.button, .button {
    box-sizing: border-box;
    font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);

    margin: 0;
    margin-left: auto;
  }
  a.button, .button {
    padding: var(--chops-button-padding);
  }
  chops-button i.material-icons, a.button i.material-icons, .button i.material-icons {
    display: block;
    margin-right: 4px;
  }
  chops-button.emphasized, a.button.emphasized, .button.emphasized {
    background: var(--chops-primary-button-bg);
    color: var(--chops-primary-button-color);

  }
  textarea, select, input {
    box-sizing: border-box;
    font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
  }
  /* Note: decoupling heading levels from styles is useful for
  * accessibility because styles will not always line up with semantically
  * appropriate heading levels.
  */
  .medium-heading {
    font-size: var(--chops-large-font-size);

        }

          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>

        <p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

<b class="line"><!---->Please READ THIS FAQ before filing a bug: https://chromium.googlesource.com<!----></b>

/chromium/src/+/HEAD/docs/security/faq.md



<b class="line"><!---->/chromium/src/+/HEAD/docs/security/faq.md<!----></b>

Please see the following link for instructions on filing security bugs:



<b class="line"><!---->Please see the following link for instructions on filing security bugs:<!----></b>



<br>





https://www.chromium.org/Home/chromium-security/reporting-security-bugs



<b class="line"><!---->https://www.chromium.org/Home/chromium-security/reporting-security-bugs<!----></b>

Reports may be eligible for reward payments under the Chrome VRP:



<b class="line"><!---->Reports may be eligible for reward payments under the Chrome VRP:<!----></b>

http://g.co/ChromeBugRewards



<b class="line"><!---->http://g.co/ChromeBugRewards<!----></b>

<b class="line"><!---->NOTE: Security bugs are normally made public once a fix has been widely<!----></b>

deployed.



<b class="line"><!---->deployed.<!----></b>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





This was reported to Brave but it also affects Chrome on Android. The original reporter asked us to report it to you.



<span class="line"><!---->This was reported to Brave but it also affects Chrome on Android. The original reporter asked us to report it to you.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Following the steps in the repro case on Android causes the autofill suggestion to cover the URL bar, making spoofing/phishing attacks easier.



<span class="line"><!---->Following the steps in the repro case on Android causes the autofill suggestion to cover the URL bar, making spoofing/phishing attacks easier.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>





 95.0.4638.69 stable



<span class="line"><!----> 95.0.4638.69 stable<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: Android



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: Android<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>





Please include a demonstration of the security bug, such as an attached



<b class="line"><!---->Please include a demonstration of the security bug, such as an attached<!----></b>



<br>





HTML or binary file that reproduces the bug when loaded in Chrome. PLEASE



<b class="line"><!---->HTML or binary file that reproduces the bug when loaded in Chrome. PLEASE<!----></b>



<br>





make the file as small as possible and remove any content not required to



<b class="line"><!---->make the file as small as possible and remove any content not required to<!----></b>



<br>





demonstrate the bug, or any personal or confidential information.



<b class="line"><!---->demonstrate the bug, or any personal or confidential information.<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





Please attach files directly, not in zip or other archive formats, and if



<b class="line"><!---->Please attach files directly, not in zip or other archive formats, and if<!----></b>



<br>





you've created a demonstration site please also attach the files needed to



<b class="line"><!---->you've created a demonstration site please also attach the files needed to<!----></b>



<br>





reproduce the demonstration locally.



<b class="line"><!---->reproduce the demonstration locally.<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





FOR CRASHES, PLEASE INCLUDE THE FOLLOWING ADDITIONAL INFORMATION



<b class="line"><!---->FOR CRASHES, PLEASE INCLUDE THE FOLLOWING ADDITIONAL INFORMATION<!----></b>



<br>





Type of crash: [tab, browser, etc.]



<b class="line"><!---->Type of crash: [tab, browser, etc.]<!----></b>



<br>





Crash State: [see link above: stack trace *with symbols*, registers,



<b class="line"><!---->Crash State: [see link above: stack trace *with symbols*, registers,<!----></b>



<br>





exception record]



<b class="line"><!---->exception record]<!----></b>



<br>





Client ID (if relevant): [see link above]



<b class="line"><!---->Client ID (if relevant): [see link above]<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





Visit 



<span class="line"><!---->Visit <!----></span>





https://kirtikumarar.com/brave/autofill.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://kirtikumarar.com/brave/autofill.html"><!---->https://kirtikumarar.com/brave/autofill.html<!----></a>



<br>





Wait until the URL has the fragment #ok



<span class="line"><!---->Wait until the URL has the fragment #ok<!----></span>



<br>





Click Anywhere on the page



<span class="line"><!---->Click Anywhere on the page<!----></span>



<br>





Note autofill covers the address bar.



<span class="line"><!---->Note autofill covers the address bar.<!----></span>

AFAIU, to calculate the position of the popup, AnchoredPopupWindow uses the window visible display frame of the mRootView[1], which is the topmost view in the current view hierarchy[2].



<span class="line"><!---->AFAIU, to calculate the position of the popup, AnchoredPopupWindow uses the window visible display frame of the mRootView[1], which is the topmost view in the current view hierarchy[2].<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





To make the Autofill Dropdown not cover URL bar, we'll need to use the web content rect instead. Maybe AnchoredPopupWindow can somehow use the provided (in the constructor) rootView for calculations?

It looks like there is a TODO in the code about this actually (line 433)?



<span class="line"><!---->It looks like there is a TODO in the code about this actually (line 433)?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





> Dave, do you recall why AnchoredPopupWindow uses rootView#getRootView for mRootView instead of directly using the rootView passed in?



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; Dave, do you recall why AnchoredPopupWindow uses rootView#getRootView for mRootView instead of directly using the rootView passed in?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





mRootView is meant to grab the root view of the window - it was years ago but I *think* I used that to guarantee people gave the actual root.



<span class="line"><!---->mRootView is meant to grab the root view of the window - it was years ago but I *think* I used that to guarantee people gave the actual root.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





> My quick take is that I could see factoring in the bounds of the provided root view when determining valid bounds for the AnchoredPopupWindow to occupy...



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; My quick take is that I could see factoring in the bounds of the provided root view when determining valid bounds for the AnchoredPopupWindow to occupy...<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





General concept sgtm.  I would just make sure we think about the implications of that View changing dimensions / moving / etc..  We might not care about it for this specific use case, but AnchoredPopupWindow is fairly general (and already handles the anchor view moving).



<span class="line"><!---->General concept sgtm.  I would just make sure we think about the implications of that View changing dimensions / moving / etc..  We might not care about it for this specific use case, but AnchoredPopupWindow is fairly general (and already handles the anchor view moving).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Another way to do this might be to pass in an optional RectProvider that gives viable bounds for the popup... that in theory would already handle any View changes automatically and can easily wrap a View.  Just an idea that might be worth trying.



<span class="line"><!---->Another way to do this might be to pass in an optional RectProvider that gives viable bounds for the popup... that in theory would already handle any View changes automatically and can easily wrap a View.  Just an idea that might be worth trying.<!----></span>

        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;

        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);

          width: 1px;
